  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_59b36b98-2a84-4652-a698-356e2c033730'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText12100639816991776478" style="display:none">Davy has always been alone. He believes that he's the only person in the world who can teleport. But what if he isn't?<br /><br />A mysterious group of people has taken Davy captive. They don't want to hire him, and they don't have any hope of appealing to him to help them. What they want is to own him. They want to use his abilities for their own purposes, whether Davy agrees to it or not. And so they set about brainwashing him and conditioning him. They have even found a way to keep a teleport captive.<br /><br />But there's one thing that they don't know. No one knows it, not even Davy. And it might save his life....</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/660508308" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/660508308?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer660508308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10137418129527265702">There's something about this series that's really sunk it's teeth into me. I already have the third book, Impulse, queued up on the iPod. There's something about this simple concept of being able to teleport that's absolutely captivating.<br/><br/>And I had misgivings going into this one. How could it top the first one? What else can you do with teleportation, right? Turns out, plenty.<br/><br/>I don't know if these are really spoilers for the first book, but I'll go ahead and warn. There are a few I guess.<br/><br/>We know </span>
  <span id="freeText10137418129527265702" style="display:none">There's something about this series that's really sunk it's teeth into me. I already have the third book, Impulse, queued up on the iPod. There's something about this simple concept of being able to teleport that's absolutely captivating.<br /><br />And I had misgivings going into this one. How could it top the first one? What else can you do with teleportation, right? Turns out, plenty.<br /><br />I don't know if these are really spoilers for the first book, but I'll go ahead and warn. There are a few I guess.<br /><br />We know Davy can teleport and he can do really cool things with it, though there are limits. He can't just go anywhere, he has to have been there, and not only that, he has to remember the place.<br /><br />By the end of book one, Davy is taking covert jobs with unnamed government entities, but of course this creates some waves. And it's a bit hard to keep it a secret after a while. Not everyone's unconscious when they're being teleported away and sometimes other people are present ... such as an entire plane full of people.<br /><br />So some "bad guys" take notice and figure out a way to keep Davy captive. These parts were extremely captivating, where Davy pushes the boundaries of his captivity while suffering tortures, you name it.<br /><br />On the other side, Millie, now Davy's wife, is stuck in the Erie (I've only 'read' these on audio, so you'll have to forgive spelling), which is the couple's home on the side of a cliff. The only way in and out is through teleportation. Sucks to be the one who can't...<br /><br />But there's a plan they put in place to get out and she follows it. I won't go into detail for fear of spoiling too much, but it works out and she's on the hunt for her beau. <br /><br />Flipping back and forth from Davy's captivity to Millie's search, the story starts to come together and lots of great teleportation ensues. <br /><br />Overall, I thought this was a great installment with lots of thought into how to keep a person captive who can teleport. I'm looking forward to continuing this story in Impulse.<br /><br />A note on the narration. Macleod Andrews once again takes the reigns here and does a commendable job. He's got the right mix of vulnerability and stubbornness that really catch the essence of Davy.<br /><br />4 out of 5 Stars (highly recommended)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10137418129527265702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_33659094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33659094" />
    <a title="Tracy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1423600-tracy"><img alt="Tracy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309535881p2/1423600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33659094?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy" href="/user/show/1423600-tracy">Tracy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33659094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2262909666413558979">Steven Gould's story development improved drastically in this sequel to Jumper. And yet, Gould stays true to his literary "voice." He graphically tells it like it is, just like you'd talk to your closest friends or speak in your inner voice. He doesn't try to find a million different synonyms for the word "butt." <br/><br/>His characters arrived fully formed, deductive, and inventive. The story line was engrossing, but I only give five stars to the books I absolutely can't put down. There were several wel</span>
  <span id="freeText2262909666413558979" style="display:none">Steven Gould's story development improved drastically in this sequel to Jumper. And yet, Gould stays true to his literary "voice." He graphically tells it like it is, just like you'd talk to your closest friends or speak in your inner voice. He doesn't try to find a million different synonyms for the word "butt." <br /><br />His characters arrived fully formed, deductive, and inventive. The story line was engrossing, but I only give five stars to the books I absolutely can't put down. There were several well thought out, deeply technical story elements that I really enjoyed. The psychoanalysis from Millie was also a major improvement from her abilities in Jumper. Overall, I look forward to reading another book from Gould, and hope he can stay both Sci-Fi and real at the same time.<br /><br />An element that didn't bother me, but might bother some of my friends is the plethura of sexual innuendo. Gould never graphically describes a sexual encounter, but the hints are there. I would most likely not recommend this book to a teenager.</span>

<div id="review_1070708431" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1070708431" />
    <a title="Richard Guion" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3982222-richard-guion"><img alt="Richard Guion" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390862833p2/3982222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1070708431?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070708431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer227482943637018264">A very good sequel to Jumper, though totally different in tone and narration. The first book was written from the 1st person perspective of Davy, who had his life turned around by the fact that he could teleport. This book is third person, split chapters between Davy and Millie, his wife. When Davy is captured, Millie discovers that she can teleport as well, although at first only in life threatening situations. Davy is captured by a pretty big and scary organization - for those who thought the </span>
  <span id="freeText227482943637018264" style="display:none">A very good sequel to Jumper, though totally different in tone and narration. The first book was written from the 1st person perspective of Davy, who had his life turned around by the fact that he could teleport. This book is third person, split chapters between Davy and Millie, his wife. When Davy is captured, Millie discovers that she can teleport as well, although at first only in life threatening situations. Davy is captured by a pretty big and scary organization - for those who thought the first book lacked a strong villain, this one certain has an antagonist. It was a page turner and lots of fun to see what Millie did with the same power that Davy has.</span>
  <a data-text-id="227482943637018264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40627509" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40627509" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1215194-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417667677p2/1215194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40627509?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/1215194-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215194-danielle?shelf=pans">pans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215194-danielle?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215194-danielle?shelf=2009-read">2009-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40627509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15035667065620541943">The first half of this book was really fun, the whole idea of creating a “reflex” in a jumper (much like Pavlov’s dog) was interesting as a training method. The latter half took a nose dive for me. <br/><br/>It seems like the two protagonists have unending knowledge about all things – so much so that it pulled me out of the story because it was odd. Like Millie knowing what type of shingles were on the roof of the house; not just that she knew what they would feel/smell like, but that she knew the name of</span>
  <span id="freeText15035667065620541943" style="display:none">The first half of this book was really fun, the whole idea of creating a “reflex” in a jumper (much like Pavlov’s dog) was interesting as a training method. The latter half took a nose dive for me. <br /><br />It seems like the two protagonists have unending knowledge about all things – so much so that it pulled me out of the story because it was odd. Like Millie knowing what type of shingles were on the roof of the house; not just that she knew what they would feel/smell like, but that she knew the name of the type of shingle. The unending description of the planes and boat using boat/plane-specific terminology that I don’t know and don’t care to know. David seems to know absolutely everything there is to know about the corrupted police and thieves around the Venezuelan airport. It was a recurring thing throughout the book and it really bothered me.<br /><br />For the record, I’m roughly the same age as Millie in the book, I’ve been with my husband for just shy of 10 years, we don’t have kids, and my training is also in psychology (though I’m working as an accountant). Now, on the complaints<br /><br />The other thing I had an issue with is how every other word out of Millie’s mouth was how badly she wanted kids. And Millie and David both spend a large portion of their inner dialogs lamenting the fact that they were unable to have sex with the other person. Really? You’ve been married 10 years and your husband (who works as a spy for the NSA) disappears, and you only miss the physical part of the relationship?? And keep droning on and on and on about it like a 16-year-old not experienced with sex? It would have been nice to see the characters mature a little bit. Sure, sex is a big thing in a relationship, but it’s not the primary reason I would miss my husband. And I wouldn’t walk by playgrounds and bemoan the fact that he didn’t “knock me up” (her words) before he got kidnapped.<br /><br />And while I’m complaining, I may as well complain about the use of the word “girlfriend” every time the characters were trying to be sassy. <br /><br />The ending was a little too neat and tidy for me too – it read like a bad rom-com movie, where everything is wrapped up neatly and the girl finally gets a baby. Bah. Two stars just because I really liked the first half of the book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15035667065620541943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34047710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34047710" />
    <a title="Brian Kristopher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1510006-brian-kristopher"><img alt="Brian Kristopher" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34047710?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Kristopher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Kristopher" href="/user/show/1510006-brian-kristopher">Brian Kristopher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34047710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5055820029693884962">This is the sequel to Jumper, which is the basis for the rather awful movie staring Hayden Christensen and Samual L. Jackson. The movie only bares a passing resemblance to the books, and both books are much better than the movie.<br/><br/>Reflex picks up ten years after Jumper. During that time, Davy has been working as a courier for the NSA. He pops in, delivers or picks up a package, and pops out. The trouble is, he'll only do the job if he knows what he's delivering, and if it won't hurt anybody.<br/><br/>Certai</span>
  <span id="freeText5055820029693884962" style="display:none">This is the sequel to Jumper, which is the basis for the rather awful movie staring Hayden Christensen and Samual L. Jackson. The movie only bares a passing resemblance to the books, and both books are much better than the movie.<br /><br />Reflex picks up ten years after Jumper. During that time, Davy has been working as a courier for the NSA. He pops in, delivers or picks up a package, and pops out. The trouble is, he'll only do the job if he knows what he's delivering, and if it won't hurt anybody.<br /><br />Certain people who know about Davy see ways his ability to teleport himself could be used to further their interests, but his scruples would get in the way. So, they drug Davy, kill is control agent and after making sure he can't teleport away, start of a program of systematic torture designed to condition him to obey their orders.<br /><br />From there, the book splits in two alternating between Davy's struggle with his kidnappers, and Millie, Davy's wife's attempts to find and rescue him.<br /><br />Reflex borrows it's basic format from the last half of Jumper, and without needing to set up the story the way the first novel does, it can spend a lot more time on the action. It's a more fun book, if a good bit shallower than Jumper. Instead of centering on Davy's efforts to get past his abusive childhood, this book is, in a way, Millie coming into her own, after spending a long time dependent on Davy.<br /><br />Both characters are a lot older in this book, a lot wiser, and for the most part, a lot smarter. Something you'd expect after ten years.<br /><br />All in all, the book is at least as good as the original, though a bit different in focus. A good read. Though, with the ending, I'd be surprised if Gould didn't have a third book in mind<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5055820029693884962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_25899377" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25899377" />
    <a title="Lisa Lap" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/174487-lisa-lap"><img alt="Lisa Lap" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1183751908p2/174487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25899377?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Lap" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Lap" href="/user/show/174487-lisa-lap">Lisa Lap</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174487-lisa-lap?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174487-lisa-lap?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/174487-lisa-lap?shelf=2011-books-read">2011-books-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25899377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14544463146977840376">This is the sequel to Jumper, the story picking up ten years after Jumper ends. In ten years, Davy and Millie haven't really done much to move forward. Yes, they're married, and yes, they travel all over the world, and yes, Davy works with the NSA as needed - but none of that is new information. Millie wants to start a family and Davy isn't sure he's ready for that. In the midst of an arguement about having children, Davy "jumps" to a meeting with his NSA contact and is consequently kidnapped. M</span>
  <span id="freeText14544463146977840376" style="display:none">This is the sequel to Jumper, the story picking up ten years after Jumper ends. In ten years, Davy and Millie haven't really done much to move forward. Yes, they're married, and yes, they travel all over the world, and yes, Davy works with the NSA as needed - but none of that is new information. Millie wants to start a family and Davy isn't sure he's ready for that. In the midst of an arguement about having children, Davy "jumps" to a meeting with his NSA contact and is consequently kidnapped. Millie is trapped in their cave home in Aerie waiting for Davy to reappear. After a day and a half of waiting she realizes something has happened and works to climb out of the cave. As she's climbing down the rope snaps and she begins to fall only to find herself on the floor of her condo. She jumped. Suddenly Davy isn't the only teleporter in the world anymore. <br /><br />How Millie can suddenly jump is never really made clear. Just as the reason that Davy is kidnapped is never really made clear. He is held in a big mansion, conditioned to jump only within the constraints his captors set forth, and only accomplishes one vague mission for them throughout the story. The NSA shuts down the investigation as it becomes clear a mysterious "Mr. Simons" is involved, the FBI continues to help Millie in her pursuits to find her husband, and Millie continues to expand her jumping skills. <br /><br />Eventually she tracks down Davy's location and manages to jump Davy to safety. Together they track down the mysterious Mr. Simons and before they can find out any information from him - he self detonates leaving us with exactly as many answers as we had when we started this book: none. <br /><br />I kept reading thinking the mystery would be solved but I was not at all satisifed by the ending which answered none of the questions the encompassed the book. I have no idea if there's a follow up to this story or not, and if there is I'm not sure if I'll read it or not. A disappointment overall. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14544463146977840376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_657865944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/657865944" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/375083-john"><img alt="John" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/657865944?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/375083-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer657865944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11494739004294207141">Reflex follows about 10 years after the first Jumper book (just called Jumper) which was way, way better than the terrible movie of the same name. Davy is doing odd jobs for the NSA, using his special teleportation skills to drop things off or pick them up, but only for good causes. Unfortunately, he gets kidnapped and his captors find a way to contain him and bend him to their will. <br/><br/>While Davy struggles to figure out his escape, his wife Millie is stunned to discover that she can teleport too. </span>
  <span id="freeText11494739004294207141" style="display:none">Reflex follows about 10 years after the first Jumper book (just called Jumper) which was way, way better than the terrible movie of the same name. Davy is doing odd jobs for the NSA, using his special teleportation skills to drop things off or pick them up, but only for good causes. Unfortunately, he gets kidnapped and his captors find a way to contain him and bend him to their will. <br /><br />While Davy struggles to figure out his escape, his wife Millie is stunned to discover that she can teleport too. Reflex uses alternating chapters to follow Davy, then Millie, then back to Davy. Millie really comes across as a hero in this book and not just a sidekick. She's a great character here; learning her own way but also using the knowledge that she's gained from ten years with Davy. <br /><br />The bad guys are believable and not just caricatures. The NSA goes from being Davy's pillar of support to Millie wondering if they're on his side at all. Everything is well developed without dragging on. <br /><br />It's been a while since I gave a book 5 stars. I thought a lot about what a 5 star rating really means. I loved this book. I didn't want to put it down, I was hooked from beginning to end, the characters were interesting and the plot moved at just the right pace. To me, that about sums it up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11494739004294207141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="This Is Not The Michael You&#39;re Looking For" class="user" itemprop="url" name="This Is Not The Michael You&#39;re Looking For" href="/user/show/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for">This Is Not The Michael You&#39;re Looking For</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/834216-this-is-not-the-michael-you-re-looking-for?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33014137" class="readable"

<div id="review_1915048146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1915048146" />
    <a title="Oatmilk Lover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41573226-oatmilk-lover"><img alt="Oatmilk Lover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605747552p2/41573226.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1915048146?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oatmilk Lover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oatmilk Lover" href="/user/show/41573226-oatmilk-lover">Oatmilk Lover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1915048146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13271033118470341616">I vaguely remember reading <i>Jumper</i> a few years back because my recollection of the entirety of the book is a little befuddled by its screen adaptation, which was only loosely based on its original material but a great movie just the same. What I do clearly remember is the novel's major theme: revenge; its protagonist David Rice: how he seemed to be a flawed yet likable character; and its plot development: how it thrilled, amazed, and kept me up for nights. I had no idea why I took—what, three yea</span>
  <span id="freeText13271033118470341616" style="display:none">I vaguely remember reading <i>Jumper</i> a few years back because my recollection of the entirety of the book is a little befuddled by its screen adaptation, which was only loosely based on its original material but a great movie just the same. What I do clearly remember is the novel's major theme: revenge; its protagonist David Rice: how he seemed to be a flawed yet likable character; and its plot development: how it thrilled, amazed, and kept me up for nights. I had no idea why I took—what, three years?—before I finally decided to read its sequel, <i>Reflex</i>. But while I'm writing down this thought, the answer came for me: When I first tried to read <i>Reflex</i> three years ago I discovered, much to my dismay, that the novel was written in third-person point of view. One of the main reasons I took delight in reading <i>Jumper</i> was spending hours being inside David Rice's head. He was hilarious as hell, and the pronoun I made the story work, since almost all of the major plot wrinkles were character-driven—that is, David Rice's doings. Hence, <i>Reflex</i> disheartened me so much that I put it away. Now, having finally plucked the courage to read it, I discovered that the old David Rice was still there, and that the third-person POV never really bothered me once because I was thankfully still in his head. <br /><br /><i>Reflex</i> is the ultimate excursion of an escapist reader. I mean, the protagonist can after all teleport. The novel, as its predecessor, took me around the world: from the most bustling streets of some city to the most scorching rocky mountains in some hemisphere in God knows exactly where. It provided me with a cheap travel without having to roll my sedentary ass out of the bed. Just like <i>Jumper</i>, it thrilled, amazed, and kept me up for nights, battling against sleep because I wanted to read through to the end at once to see how things would come to a conclusion. At the end, finally, <i>Reflex</i> did not disappoint. It maintained its fast pace and blew shit up until its closing stages. Hell, the only chapter that was particularly calm was the last one, with David and Millie happy together after their separation. <br /><br />At times <i>Reflex</i> could be painfully funny as well just like <i>Jumper</i>. The characters are well-developed and as human as possible. Ironically, I admire the set of antagonists: Lawrence Simons, Hyacinth Pope, Padgett, Dr. Conley. They seemed at first to be the usual band of bad guys operating under greed for power and money, but there is far more in them than what the book gives away in the first few chapters. Later, the veils go down one character at a time, and their true motivations are revealed. Then I gradually sympathized with them and could only feel sadness about their actions, which brings me to another good point in the book that the psychology major in me liked best. <br /><br />Operant Conditioning is a method in learning that emphasizes reward and punishment in behavior. For example, when a child's actions result to pleasant consequences, the child will likely behave similarly in the future; when the child's actions result to unpleasant consequences, the child will likely not repeat the actions. In <i>Reflex</i>, David Rice went through an intensive operant conditioning to succumb to his enemies' demands. Again, I am awed by Steven Gould's vision to see through his characters. He knows so well that his protagonist cannot be lulled by money, so he had his antagonists condition him instead. Hence, the title <i>Reflex</i>. <br /><br />Steven Gould is probably the only person in the world who could take in global issues in his writing without boring his readers to tears. He leaves out things that his readers will unlikely understand and instead focuses on the things that will draw his readers' attention. Unlike most writers, he does not try to impress anyone that he knows things concerning our society. Also, the way he writes is no-nonsense. His prose may never be referred to as good, but it is crisp enough to deliver action—and that's the only thing Gould really needs, to be honest.<br /><br /><i>Reflex</i> by Steven Gould is highly recommended for science fiction-action fans, or anyone who plainly wants a heart-pounding read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13271033118470341616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2455344639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2455344639" />
    <a title="J. Peters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4064193-j-peters"><img alt="J. Peters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530681369p2/4064193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2455344639?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J. Peters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J. Peters" href="/user/show/4064193-j-peters">J. Peters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9289175-reflex">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2455344639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18366272389755012172">Jumper is one of my favorite books and I've read it numerous times now. I've read Reflex a couple of times, and I'm in the process of rereading Impulse, which I've only read once before. I haven't read Exo yet, but that will be next on my list. <br/><br/>So far, Reflex is my least favorite of the series. <br/><br/>It's not that it's poorly written - quite the opposite in fact. It's very well written, with some fun side characters and great character moments for both Davy and Millie.<br/><br/>My main problem is, well, I didn'</span>
  <span id="freeText18366272389755012172" style="display:none">Jumper is one of my favorite books and I've read it numerous times now. I've read Reflex a couple of times, and I'm in the process of rereading Impulse, which I've only read once before. I haven't read Exo yet, but that will be next on my list. <br /><br />So far, Reflex is my least favorite of the series. <br /><br />It's not that it's poorly written - quite the opposite in fact. It's very well written, with some fun side characters and great character moments for both Davy and Millie.<br /><br />My main problem is, well, I didn't enjoy reading about torture for that long.<br /><br />It's kind of an uncomfortable read. The book goes into detail on the kind of hell that Davy experiences while in the hands of his kidnappers, and it's difficult to read. I tended to skim through those parts this time around. <br /><br />My favorite parts of the book were those dealing with Millie and her ongoing search for Davy. Through her, the old spirit of the Jumper book still shined. <br /><br />One of the things I liked most about Jumper was that it had a sense of adventure and wonder, while still dealing with a lot of heavy topics and doing an impressive juggling act for them. And that's missing here, at least, it's missing from Davy's sections. The fact that both Davy and Millie are written from a third-person POV this time (Davy was first-person in the first book) doesn't help much. <br /><br />I think a part of that is that Davy spends most of the book in one general area, while Millie is actively working towards a goal. Her parts of the book were more fun, and I kinda wish the book had spent more time focusing on her, as that's where the meat of the story was for me. I think it could've helped add tension and mystery to the book. As the reader, you know where Davy is and what's happening to him - Millie doesn't. So when the book switches to Millie, it can be a little frustrating as she's trying to play catch up. But if the book had only been told from mostly Millie's perspective (say after the meeting with Cox, it then stays with Millie until towards the end), I think it would've greatly enhanced that feeling of tension and mystery. Then, everything that Millie discovers would be new to the reader as well. Millie's chapters had more of a sense of fun and adventure in them. One of the things I loved about the first book was Davy's dry sense of humor in tough situations. Like, when he's forced to jump out of the NSA office and he says "We mean no harm to your planet." He knows it's probably not gonna help his cause at all, but it's a funny moment that's true to his character. In this one, because of the extreme situation he's found himself in, that's kind of lost. Millie, though she's desperate in her search and it's not exactly a fun point of her life, at least has the freedom of interacting with a variety of characters and has some pretty great moments of dry humor herself. <br /><br />I don't mind that the book doesn't flinch away from showing the gruesome stuff - it's just not something that really appeals to me. If I reread this in the future, I'll likely skim or skip those parts entirely.<br /><br />I also didn't care for Hyacinth Pope much at all. Her character just feels kind of awkward. <br /><br />I am looking forward to finishing the series. From what I recall, Impulse is more of a return to roots kind of book. I have no idea about Exo yet, but I'm hoping for the best.</span>

  <span id="freeText9365328107295305843" style="display:none"> I first watched the movie and liked it, so I was interested in reading the book, because the books are always better than the movies, right..? But I was disappointed.<br /><br />The first book : Jumper, was enjoyable. I liked it because there wasn’t an “enemy” that wants to kill David, it was like a book about a normal kid (except the fact that he can teleport) living is life. That made the book more realistic and representative of a real life. But for the same reason, I wasn’t thrilled to continue reading.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />I didn’t like the second book : Reflex. I was raging against the “bad guys” the hole book, and because of that I didn’t enjoy the reading. It was too morbid (not sure if it is the right word). There were too much unanswered questions : Why can Millie jump? Who is the leader of the “bad guys”? And something I didn’t like at the end : They will have children, that is so stupid, they can’t even have a real life because of the “bad guys” and they want to give birth to a kid that won’t be able to have a normal life.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Finally I don’t regret my reading, but wouldn’t recommand the books. I first thought the book would be the movie plot but with explanation but it was a whole other story. I wouldn’t say the movie was better because it wasn’t the same story. I would have prefered a book about the Paladins chasing David though.<br /><br />Max</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11828442090237402961">Have you ever imagined yourself to be a character in a book? Have you ever said, ooh yes, I wanna be him. Or, blindfuckme, that guy is so totally me! <br/><br/>Reflex is one of those books that's like wine. You write a sequel years later and boy, it's gold. You can read about a book of a teenager and go through his stumbles because you know, you've been through his age. You've been a teen. So when I read the first book, I transported myself to the past and read it with the eager hunger of a teenager who k</span>
  <span id="freeText11828442090237402961" style="display:none">Have you ever imagined yourself to be a character in a book? Have you ever said, ooh yes, I wanna be him. Or, blindfuckme, that guy is so totally me! <br /><br />Reflex is one of those books that's like wine. You write a sequel years later and boy, it's gold. You can read about a book of a teenager and go through his stumbles because you know, you've been through his age. You've been a teen. So when I read the first book, I transported myself to the past and read it with the eager hunger of a teenager who knows exactly what's happening. And that is nothing. <br /><br />Reflex is the story of the hero of Jumper. Only it's ten years later and he's ten years older. I'm 28 now and I can tell you, it's like watching myself in the present. Only he's married while I'm still struggling to get over my ex and he has cool powers. <br /><br />There are two more books but I'm not going to read them for a while. It's not Davy's story anymore. It's not mine anymore. And i don't know what should I pick up. I'm still not over the ending. I'm still not over a lot of things. <br /><br />Who would've thought this one would've been an eye opener of sorts. Hah. <br /><br />If you're reading this expecting a review, oh well, be disappointed.</span>

        <a title="Kel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kel" href="/user/show/9598370-kel">Kel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes realistic action, and a little bit of sci-fi</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9598370-kel?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9598370-kel?shelf=sci-fi-ish">sci-fi-ish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer497190999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer380253786785343257">A sequel to the book (and movie) Jumper, Reflex throws us back into the lives of Davey (who can 'jump' to anywhere in the world he can see or has visited before, just by thinking about it) and his wife Millie, in the present day.<br/><br/>Davey is working for the NSA on the quiet in sensitive cases like kidnapping and extraction, and his wife is a counsellor. Very quickly, their lives are upended when Davey - who has no limits on where he can go in an instant - is kidnapped, and can't escape.<br/><br/>This is a gre</span>
  <span id="freeText380253786785343257" style="display:none">A sequel to the book (and movie) Jumper, Reflex throws us back into the lives of Davey (who can 'jump' to anywhere in the world he can see or has visited before, just by thinking about it) and his wife Millie, in the present day.<br /><br />Davey is working for the NSA on the quiet in sensitive cases like kidnapping and extraction, and his wife is a counsellor. Very quickly, their lives are upended when Davey - who has no limits on where he can go in an instant - is kidnapped, and can't escape.<br /><br />This is a great read, with believable action, a strong female lead in Millie, twists that are hard to see coming and kept me up late reading way past my intended bedtime. Also, the characters are a bit sarcastic by nature, so there's some great snark and comebacks throughout the tale.<br /><br />I really enjoyed it, so much that I'm going to read more by Steven Gould.</span>
  <a data-text-id="380253786785343257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3559993601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3559993601" />
    <a title="Gareth Otton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8925316-gareth-otton"><img alt="Gareth Otton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551041676p2/8925316.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3559993601?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gareth Otton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gareth Otton" href="/user/show/8925316-gareth-otton">Gareth Otton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3559993601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15641968391801886127">I have to admit that my absolute favourite type of story involving a person with awesome super powers is to lock them in a scenario where they can't use those powers properly for nearly a whole book. I mean, what could be more enjoyable than watching someone with superpowers act like a normal human being? The only way you could make that better would be if you subject the reader to countless chapters of that protagonist they like so much being tortured... That's a genius idea.<br/><br/>In case it isn't cl</span>
  <span id="freeText15641968391801886127" style="display:none">I have to admit that my absolute favourite type of story involving a person with awesome super powers is to lock them in a scenario where they can't use those powers properly for nearly a whole book. I mean, what could be more enjoyable than watching someone with superpowers act like a normal human being? The only way you could make that better would be if you subject the reader to countless chapters of that protagonist they like so much being tortured... That's a genius idea.<br /><br />In case it isn't clear in written form, I may have indulged in a touch of sarcasm in that opening paragraph.<br /><br />I <b>HATED</b> this book. Its like someone asked me at the end of the last novel all the things I didn't want to happen in this novel and then they went and wrote a novel by ticking every single item off that list. <br /><br />The fun adventurous tone that made the first novel great is replaced by the darker, melancholy tone that the worst parts of the first novel toyed with. This book stats in a place of doom and gloom, then goes downhill from there. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Our protagonist who has the power to teleport anywhere in the world spends most of the novel locked in one location being tortured both physically and psychologically.<br /><br />Meanwhile, his wife had apparently caught ability to teleport like some sexually transmitted disease, and we are stuck watching her learn all the same lessons that Davey learned in the first book. Not only was this tedious as all hell, but it reduces what is special about Davey. One of the big strengths of the 1st book was that as far as we knew Davey was the only person in the world who could do this amazing thing. It made it feel unique and special. His wife learning how to do it with zero explanation as to why cheapens that considerably.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Easily the worst thing about this novel though is the discomfort. The trials of the protagonist, the drawn out plot, the inescapable situations and the constant dreariness of the tone just made my skin crawl. I could never get comfortable reading this.<br /><br />However, for all that, I'm aware that most of these points are subjective. I think me and the author just had very different ideas about where to take this series. So from that point of view and trying to be fair in this review, I'm adding 2 starts because I think that different readers with different desires might enjoy this much more than I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15641968391801886127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3436338272" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3436338272" />
    <a title="Bishop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59610111-bishop"><img alt="Bishop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570279841p2/59610111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3436338272?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bishop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bishop" href="/user/show/59610111-bishop">Bishop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9289175-reflex">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3436338272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer37839081397742833">Reflex is a fantastic followup to Jumper, but it suffers from a few differences which make it enjoyable in a decidedly different way. Gould's consistency and attention to detail in his development of the "jumper" superpower is thorough and engaging. The flaws he gives the Jumper are not lazy kryptonite, but genuinely interesting foils to his capabilities. Furthermore, Gould imbues his intrigues with suspense and heart-pounding action.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, there were some elements from Jumper that I mis</span>
  <span id="freeText37839081397742833" style="display:none">Reflex is a fantastic followup to Jumper, but it suffers from a few differences which make it enjoyable in a decidedly different way. Gould's consistency and attention to detail in his development of the "jumper" superpower is thorough and engaging. The flaws he gives the Jumper are not lazy kryptonite, but genuinely interesting foils to his capabilities. Furthermore, Gould imbues his intrigues with suspense and heart-pounding action.<br /><br />Unfortunately, there were some elements from Jumper that I missed in this novel. In the first book I was primarily engaged by the way that Davy's personal development intersected with his fantastical ability. Reflex leans much more heavily into action and intrigue, with the main characters operating more or less as given throughout the entire novel. In that sense, this followup novel is skewed more towards science fiction than its predecessor.<br /><br />There were a couple of elements which I found mildly disagreeable as well. I am not so prudish that I can't enjoy a novel with sex in it, but Gould's deployment here struck me as a bit obsessive and fetishistic. If it were a standalone novel I would assume that these moments were merely titillatory, but in context with Jumper I'm guessing that there is a moral here about fidelity and longing which I don't think was adequately communicated.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Millie's development into a jumper was also quite disappointing. I was very interested to see how she dealt with her newfound power, especially given how different her character is from Davy, but in the end her journey was an approximate caricature of Davy's. Much of Millie's character was sacrificed in the interest of pushing the main plot arc forward at a steady clip.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Regardless, Reflex is excellent, and I appreciate that the author did not focus on recreating Jumper, but instead took the risk of pivoting slightly in format to keep his subject compelling. I am looking forward to reading the rest of the novels in the Jumper universe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="37839081397742833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2271463687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2271463687" />
    <a title="Nico A Klein" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43569903-nico-a-klein"><img alt="Nico A Klein" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595189826p2/43569903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2271463687?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nico A Klein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nico A Klein" href="/user/show/43569903-nico-a-klein">Nico A Klein</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9289175-reflex">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2271463687&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2271463687" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18030542361960367664">I started reading this in January and it took me until October to finish mostly because it was a chore for me to really get into it. I read the first one and enjoyed it for what it was but that’s about it. As for Reflex... I only read it so I could be done with it. The writing was lacking and didn’t hold my attention like most other books I’ve read. The author has this thing for the word “shuddered” as it’s so over used in both the first book and this one. <br/><br/>At a certain point you kind of came to </span>
  <span id="freeText18030542361960367664" style="display:none">I started reading this in January and it took me until October to finish mostly because it was a chore for me to really get into it. I read the first one and enjoyed it for what it was but that’s about it. As for Reflex... I only read it so I could be done with it. The writing was lacking and didn’t hold my attention like most other books I’ve read. The author has this thing for the word “shuddered” as it’s so over used in both the first book and this one. <br /><br />At a certain point you kind of came to expect the Hyacinth Pope character to always come on to Davy any time she’s in the room with him. Either have him cave or refuse her right off and be done with it. She drugs him at one point and you kind of have to think that she’s hella desperate or Davy is just that sexually attractive to her. I dunno. <br /><br />I will agree with other reviewers about Millie’s internal dialog concerning wanting a baby and how repetitive that becomes. <br /><br />When I got down to the last 20mins of the book, I was literally falling asleep. I’m glad I finished it though so I don’t have to worry about reading any more of it. 🤷🏻‍♂️</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14747552472012756693">2.5 stars<br/><br/>There were many things I disliked about this. <br/>The fact that Millie now jumps bugs me so much. She has never done it before and suddenly she's able to do it? Is teleportation like the flu, you can "catch" it? WTH?<br/>I got so sick of the sex/baby stuff. Ugh. Davy has been kidnapped and Mille takes the time to think "I wish he'd knocked me up first?" Or what about "Come home soon, Davy, I need to get laid?" Really? I mean, really?!?   <span id="freeText14747552472012756693" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />There were many things I disliked about this. <br />The fact that Millie now jumps bugs me so much. And Davy was thinking about it, too, but not as bad. It just really aggravated me. <br />The storyline itself was okay. I would have enjoyed it more, I think, had Millie not been given 1/2 the book in her POV. I've already read a book about learning to jump so reading it again through her eyes was meh. <br /><br />Reflex was okay. Not as good as Jumper but okay.<br /></span>

Davy gets kidnapped (and... brace yourself... tortured in rather horrible ways), and Millie is left to solve the crime. Like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47970.Jumper__Jumper___1_' title='Jumper (Jumper, #1) by Steven Gould' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jumper</a>, the story here is the plot, not the characterization. Aside from the nausea, I couldn't really bring myself to</span>
  <span id="freeText3721400018262054218" style="display:none">Another adventure with Davy, ten years after the previous book. Davy's got an established career with the NSA, and his girlfriend-now-wife Millie gets transported all over the globe by Davy's unlimited teleporting ability. But sure enough, trouble strikes. Davy gets kidnapped (and... brace yourself... tortured in rather horrible ways), and Millie is left to solve the crime. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47970.Jumper__Jumper___1_" title="Jumper (Jumper, #1) by Steven Gould" rel="nofollow noopener">Jumper</a>, the story here is the plot, not the characterization. Aside from the nausea, I couldn't really bring myself to feel what the characters felt. But it's quite a gripping story, and I was rooting for an escape, and I liked that in the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it took both of them to solve it <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. </span>

<div id="review_2652770475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2652770475" />
    <a title="Taid Stone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64878424-taid-stone"><img alt="Taid Stone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538683336p2/64878424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2652770475?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taid Stone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taid Stone" href="/user/show/64878424-taid-stone">Taid Stone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2652770475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17884780904043521033">Ten years passes between the first novel "Jumper" and "Reflex." It is possible to read this book before the first, but many details will not make as much sense. Davy, the teleporter, is married for example. And, he works for a few government agencies who pay him well for contracted jobs. However, it is people from the various agencies and more secretive groups who give the novel conflicts, interesting ones. Several themes are important in this book. Clearly with Davy being married, love plays a </span>
  <span id="freeText17884780904043521033" style="display:none">Ten years passes between the first novel "Jumper" and "Reflex." It is possible to read this book before the first, but many details will not make as much sense. Davy, the teleporter, is married for example. And, he works for a few government agencies who pay him well for contracted jobs. However, it is people from the various agencies and more secretive groups who give the novel conflicts, interesting ones. Several themes are important in this book. Clearly with Davy being married, love plays a big role. Revenge for slights against people is even more important, less for specific actions and more for motivations to act. Finally, despite having a loving wife, Davy wants another jumper who can identify with him. <br /><br />The novel is well plotted. Enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17884780904043521033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2590450449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2590450449" />
    <a title="Anthony Pinos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84195828-anthony-pinos"><img alt="Anthony Pinos" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2590450449?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Pinos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Pinos" href="/user/show/84195828-anthony-pinos">Anthony Pinos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2590450449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5270397735958712636">I loved the perspective shift from just Davy to both Davy and Millie. Personally I love it when stories have two protagonists and switch between the two. I enjoyed this one more than the first one, although I felt as though the plot flowed better in the first one. Much like the first one, I liked how Gould wrote the characters. He did so in a way that made it feel like normal people in extraordinary stories. The science however was pretty shaky and the antagonists were pretty underdeveloped. Tow</span>
  <span id="freeText5270397735958712636" style="display:none">I loved the perspective shift from just Davy to both Davy and Millie. Personally I love it when stories have two protagonists and switch between the two. I enjoyed this one more than the first one, although I felt as though the plot flowed better in the first one. Much like the first one, I liked how Gould wrote the characters. He did so in a way that made it feel like normal people in extraordinary stories. The science however was pretty shaky and the antagonists were pretty underdeveloped. Towards the end of the novel the story also seemed to drag on. All in all, Reflex was an enjoyable followup to Jumper and I had fun with it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5270397735958712636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RbY8KqS1HkqLYFW4UOnHW4w8HSgWgAphLCEbga8wjapiAsRfn3bqbzHiGHflVUurv/ceWTkAQpVRekcDREDmsg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('a8P5UiesBooLoP0mtz+4AmZt1C3bGzJXtFOQl+742vxMdwEnHG/yr7EisOkCgzTyVabXXPSbeqPJCMwVBYix5A==')})
  }

While death from mortal wounds is still possible, life is made easier in a socially liberated society where automation and income equality allow passion pursuits to flourish over traditional work. If she succeeds, she’ll assume her Original’s place in society. If she fails, her life will end. Holly’s progress is monitored by an assigned contact that feeds her information as she confronts the blank, robotic world around her, discovering that others view life through the theme of their own choosing. \n\nWith her newly implanted combat and deduction skills, Holly fends off both attacks by terrorists and doubts about her own trustworthiness as clues lead her to her Original - and to the truth about Jonathan. Written by the creator of Tcl and Tk, this book is the single authoritative resource for anyone who wants to work with this extraordinary environment. The book offers an introduction and overview of Tcl and Tk and then presents detailed instructions for script writing in Tcl and working with the Tk toolkit. You will discover how Tk\'s windowing shell, wish, enables you to develop window-based applications with amazingly few lines of code. You will also find information on Tk\'s novel and powerful facility for linking applications. Many other features are also described, such as Tk\'s hypertext and hypergraphics widgets and Tcl\'s facilities for procedures, list management, and subprocess execution. For interested readers, the book also describes the C interfaces for Tcl and Tk, showing how to extend their built-in features by writing new C commands.
